+Jamison Brereton

91
Soma
Gotama R─Бh┼лgaс╣Зa
23 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh 1тАУ4, g─Бyatr─л 5тАУ16, uс╣гс╣Зih 17, triс╣гс╣нubh 18тАУ23
Long and metrically disunified, this hymn no doubt falls into distinct segments, but there is no scholarly agreement about the exact divisions. Some verse groupings are found together in later liturgical texts (e.g., vss. 16тАУ18, which, though in three dif ferent meters, agree in contents), but in other cases there is no external evidence. It is possible that the triс╣гс╣нubh verses at the beginning (vss. 1тАУ4) and those at the end (vss. 19тАУ23) belong together, with the dimeter verses 5тАУ16 (plus 17тАУ18) having been inserted between them. This is suggested by the fact that verse 19 starts with the same sequence as the beginning of verse 4 (y─Б╠Б te dh─Б╠Бm─Бni), and also by the apparent ring between 1a pr├б cikitaс╕е and 23d pr├б cikits─Б.
In any case this hymn shares both the rather simplified rhetoric and the totalizing thematics of GotamaтАЩs hymns to the All Gods. Soma is identified with numerous224 I.91
gods (see, e.g., vss. 3, 5) and is credited with multiple cosmogonic deeds (e.g., vs. 22) and martial powers (e.g., vs. 21). Especially in the g─Бyatr─л verses he is begged for all sorts of aid and comradeship.
Since this is not a Soma Pavam─Бna hymn and is not found in the IXth Maс╣Зс╕Нala, the ritual details that dominate that maс╣Зс╕Нala are essentially absent here. The exception is the aforementioned triad of verses 16тАУ18, each of which contains a form of ─Б╠Б тИЪpy─Б тАЬswell,тАЭ an idiom used of the soaking of the soma stalks in water to make them swell up before their pressing. As this action occurs before the puri
fication process proper, it is hardly mentioned in the IXth Maс╣Зс╕Нala (twice in fact, once [IX.31.4] in an exact repetition of the present vs. 16 in a hymn attributed to our poet Gotama R─Бh┼лgaс╣Зa), while it is the most prominent ritual detail in this hymn.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Soma, are thoroughly apprehended by our understanding; you lead us along a straight path; by your guidance, Indra, our righteous fathers obtained wealth among the gods.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

You, Soma, have become conspicuous through our inspired thought. YouтАФlead along the straightest path.
Through your guidance, o drop, our insightful forefathers had their
share in the treasure among the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The multiple possible meanings of the root(s) тИЪcit and the unclear morphological identity of (pr├б) cikitaс╕е make the interpretation of the first p─Бda somewhat difficult. I follow ThiemeтАЩs solution (Plusq.), adopted also by K├╝mmel (176-77), that it is underlyingly a medial injunctive to the perfect stem (that is, an unaugmented pluperfect), patterning with pf. cikit├й, etc. But the underspecification of this posited

*cikita caused it to be re-marked with an active ending (like root presents of the type aduha-t). It should not be a subjunctive, despite its thematic appearance, because of the zero-grade root syllable, and, pace Witzel Got┼Н, it should not be a trans./caus.

reduplicated aorist because of the light reduplicating syllable (expect *c─лkitas) – although I do have to admit that acikitat in VII.80.2 does seem to function like a redupl. aorist. Witzel Got┼Н supply panth─Б╠Бm, from b, as object in a, but this seems unnecessary. On a potential ring made by pr├б cikitaс╕е here and pr├б cikits─Б in the last p─Бda of the hymn (23d), see published introduction. The other question in p─Бda a is whose inspired thought is at issue. I assume that it is ours (that is, the poetsтАЩ), in that the priests and poets create the ritual that makes soma manifest.

Our wise forefathers by thy guidance, Indu, dealt out among the Gods their share of treasure.

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Soma, are the doer of good by holy acts; you are powerful by your energies, and know all things; you are the showerer (of benefits) by your bounties, and (are great) by your greatness; you, the guide of men, has been well nourished by sacrificial offerings.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

You, Soma, become very intent through your intentions; very skillful with your skills, all-knowing.
You are a bull through your bullish powers, your greatness. You became brilliant through your brilliancies, drawing the gaze of men.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse is structured by a series of etymological figures involving a nom. sg. modifying soma and an instr. pl. specifying his qualities – a: kr├бtubhiс╕е sukr├бtuс╕е, b: d├бkс╣гaiс╕е sud├бkс╣гaс╕е, c: vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б vс╣Ыс╣гatv├йbhiс╕е, d: dyumn├йbhir dyumn─л╠Б. It is a not a subtle device, but effective. On the first hemistich see further ad vs. 14.

+Griffith

Thou by thine insight art most wise, O Soma, strong by thine energies and all possessing,
Mighty art thou by all thy powers and greatness, by glories art thou glorious, guide of mortals.

+Geldner

Du, Soma, bist an Einsicht wohleinsichtig, an Verstand wohlverst├дndig, du der Allwissende. Du bist ein Bulle an Bullenst├дrke, an Gr├╢├Яe; du mit dem Herrenauge wardst glanzreich an Glanz.

+Grassmann

Durch Einsicht bist du einsichtsvoll, o Soma, durch Kr├дfte kr├дftig, du der Allbesitzer; Ein Stier bist du durch Stiereskraft und Gr├╢sse, durch Reichthum wurdest reich du M├дnnerschauer.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYour acts are (like those) of the royal Varuс╣Зa; your glory, Soma, is great and profound; you are the purifier (of all), like the beloved Mitra; you are the augmenter of all, like Aryaman.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

R─Бj├▒o varuс╣Зasya: y─Бg─Бrtham ─Бhс╣Ыtaс╕е kс╣Ыto vastreс╣З─Бvс╣Ыtaс╕е soma varuс╣Зaс╕е: varuс╣Зa means that which is enclosed in a cloth, or the Soma which has been purchased for a sacrifice. soma asm─Бkam br─Бhmaс╣З─Бn─Бm r─Бj─Б, soma is the king of the br─Бhmaс╣Зas (Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 1.8.10.2); somaraj─Бno br─Бhmaс╣Зaс╕е, the br─Бhmaс╣Зas have soma for king

+Jamison Brereton

The commandments of King Varuс╣Зa are yours; lofty and deep is your domain, o Soma.
You are blazing pure, like dear Mitra. You are besought for skill like Aryaman, o Soma.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Soma is here identified with the three principal ─Аdityas. This vs. is identical to IX.88.8, though the two published translation differ in p─Бda b. I would now alter the tr. here to тАЬyours is his lofty, deep domain, o Soma.тАЭ See disc. ad IX.88.8.

The (pseudo-)gerundive dakс╣г─Б╠Бyya- has attracted a number of different renderings – in this passage alone, Geldner тАЬzu Gunst geneigt,тАЭ Renou тАЬquтАЩon doit-servirefficacement,тАЭ Witzel Got┼Н тАЬals Zufriedenzustellender.тАЭ I prefer to tie it more closely with d├бkс╣гa- тАШskillтАЩ, as тАЬwhose skill is to be sought,тАЭ despite the awkwardness of the English gloss. In this passage Soma was just credited with skill (2b) and will later dispense it (7c; cf. also 14c), and in both I.129.2 and VII.97.8 the ability of Indra and Bс╣Ыhaspati to bring about good things is emphasized. JPB in VII.1.2 prefers тАЬto be skillfully tended,тАЭ quite close to RenouтАЩs rendering above. This latter tr. would work for Agni (II.4.3, VII.1.2), who requires ritual tending, but less well for Indra, Bс╣Ыhaspati, and (here) Aryaman.

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬEndowed with all the glories (that are displayed) by you in heaven, on earth, in the mountains, in the plural nts, in the waters, do you, illustrious Soma, well-disposed towards us, and devoid of anger, accept our oblations.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Illustrious Soma = royal (r─Бjan) soma

+Jamison Brereton

Your domains that are in heaven, that are on the earth, that are in the mountains, in the plants, in the watersтАФ
with all those, being well-disposed and not angry, King Soma, accept our oblations.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The perennially difficult dh─Б╠Бman-, found also in 3b, is a bit difficult to interpret here as well. In both 3b and 4ab, the dh─Б╠Бman- appear to be concrete and locatable in space, for which the tr. тАШdomain(s)тАЩ fits well (cf. also Witzel Got┼Н тАЬSt├дttenтАЭ). But then in cd Soma is urged to accept our oblations with them, which seems difficult to do with a place and edges closer to GeldnerтАЩs тАЬFormen,тАЭ a nebulous and all-purpose rendering that I try to avoid with this word. RenouтАЩs тАЬstructuresтАЭ doesnтАЩt help either. I must assume that тАЬaccept with all your (domains)тАЭ is a compressed way of saying тАЬwherever you are, accept.тАЭ The same problem is found, to some extent, in vs. 19.

With all thy glories on the earth, in heaven, on mountains, in the plants, and in the waters,–
With all of these, well-pleased and not in anger, accept, O royal Soma, our oblations.

Satpatis tvam r─Бj─Б uta: sat may also mean br─Бhmaс╣Зa, hence: the protector, or lord (pati), or the king (r─Бj─Б of the br─Бhmaс╣Зas); you are holy sacrifice: Soma is identified with the sacrifice, from the essential part it performs in it: tadr┼лpo bhavanti s─Бdhyatv─Бd yaj├▒─Бn─Бm

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Soma, fond of praise, the lord of plural nts, are life to us; if you will, we shall not die.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Somo v─Б oс╣гadh─лn─Бm r─Бj─Б (Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 6.1.9.1)

+Jamison Brereton

And if you will wish us to live, Soma, we will not die.
(You are) the lord of the forest to whom praise is dear.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

A good example of subordinating ca.

On the use of v├бnasp├бti- тАШlord of the forestтАЩ for soma, see comm. ad IX.12.7.

This usage is found only here and in IX.12.7. Because our phrase priy├бstotro v├бnasp├бtiс╕е is almost identical to IX.12.7 n├нtyastotro v├бnasp├бtiс╕е, I am now inclined to translate the bahuvr. тАШwho has praise as his ownтАЩ, not тАШto whom praise is dearтАЩ.

Praise-loving Lord of plants art thou.

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAccepting this our sacrifice, and this our praise, approach, Soma, and be to us as the augmenter of our rite.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

This sacrifice hereтАФhaving delighted in this speech, come near to it. Soma, be (ready) to strengthen us.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I take the pf. part. jujuс╣г─Бс╣З├бс╕е as expressing an action anterior to that of the main verb, impv. up─Б╠Бgahi. If this is correct, the verse is constructed chiastically, with im├бс╣Г yaj├▒├бm construed with up─Б╠Бgahi, while the call that precedes SomaтАЩs arrival at the sacrifice is nested in between (id├бс╣Г v├бco, jujuс╣г─Бn├бс╕е).

+Griffith

Accepting this our sacrifice and this our praise, O Soma, come,
And be thou nigh to prosper us.

An diesem Opfer, an dieser Rede dich erfreuend komm herbei! Sei du, Soma, uns zum Gedeihen!

+Grassmann

Lass dieses Opfer, dieses Lied gefallen dir und komm herbei, O Soma, du sei uns zum Heil.

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe experienced sage commends the mortal who, through affection, divine Soma, praises you.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

O Soma, the mortal who will take pleasure in your comradeship, o god, him does skill accompany, him does the sage poet.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Although it is tempting to take d├бkс╣гa- as adjectival here (so Geldner, Witzel Got┼Н), I am somewhat dubious that this stem can be an adjective, and in any case the emphasis on the skill associated with Soma in this hymn (vss. 2b, 3d, 7c) suggests a nominal reading here. Although the pairing of an abstract quality (skill) with an animate being (poet) might seem awkward, I see it as a variant reprise of 2ab, where kr├бtu- (тАШintentionтАЩ) and d├бkс╣гa- were paired; as discussed ad I.2.7-9, kr├бtu- and d├бkс╣гa- are two of the three qualities required to bring an action about and are regularly associated. Here kav├н- stands in for kr├бtu-. This substitution is enabled by the syntagm тАЬthe poetтАЩs kr├бtu-, as in the cmpd. kav├н-kratu-. (RenouтАЩs interpr. is similar; see his n.)

+Griffith

O Soma, God, the mortal man who in thy friendship hath delight,
Him doth the mighty Sage befriend.

+Geldner

Welcher Sterbliche, o Gott Soma, in deiner Gesellschaft gern verweilt, dem steht der wirksame Seher zur Seite.

+Grassmann

Welch Sterblicher, o Gott, sich freut, o Soma, deiner Br├╝derschaft, Dem ist der starke Seher hold.

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the milky juices flow around you; may sacrificial offerings and vigour be concentrated in the destroyer of foes; and, being fully nourished, do you provide, Soma, excellent viands in heaven for our immortality.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Let your milk-drinks come together and together your prizes, together the bullish powers of you who vanquish hostility.
Swelling up for the immortal, Soma, establish your own highest
measures of fame in heaven.

+Griffith

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhichever of your glories (men) worship with oblations, may our sacrifice be invested with them all; come to our mansions, Soma, who are the bestower of wealth, the transporter (over difficulties); attended by valiant heroes, the non-destroyer of progeny.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Those domains of yours that they sacrifice to with oblation, let all these of yours be encompassing the sacrifice.
Fattening the livestock, furthering (us), bringing good heroes, not
smiting heroes, o Soma, advance to our doorways.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Here again, as in vs. 4, the dh─Б╠Бm─Бni of Soma are recipients of the oblation; GeldnerтАЩs Formen again works more smoothly, but I still consider these to be the locales listed in 4ab, each of which can be a site of sacrifice.

Note the disharmony in number between the neut. pl. subj. (t─Б╠Бvi┼Ыv─Б) and the sg. pred. nom. (paribh┼л╠Бс╕е) and verb (astu). This could be an example of the inherited construction of neuter pl. with a singular verb, but I think itтАЩs more likely just a constructio ad sensum, with тАЬall theseтАЭ summarizing the plural subjects of the rel. cl.

as if in a mass. English тАЬall thisтАЭ can be similarly used, after a listing of discrete entities. The Sanskrit has just been more punctilious about maintaining number agreement.

Geldner, Renou, Witzel Got┼Н all supply тАШlifetimeтАЩ as the implicit object of prat├бraс╣Зaс╕е, rather than my тАШusтАЩ; they are most likely correct, given how common the idiom ─Б╠Бyus- pr├б тИЪtс╣Э is. I might change the published translation to тАЬlengthening (our lifetime).тАЭ

+Griffith

Such of thy glories as with poured oblations men honour, may they all invest our worship.
Wealth-giver, furtherer with troops of heroes, sparing the brave, come, Soma, to our houses.

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTo him who present (offerings), Soma gives a cow, a swift horse, and a son who is able in affairs, skilful in domestic concerns, assiduous in worship, eminent in society, and who is an honour to his father.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Soma gives a milk-cow, Soma a swift steed, Soma a hero fit for actionтАФ one fit for the residence, for the rite, for the assembly, one who brings fame to the forefathersтАФ(gives these to the man) who will do ritual service to him.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) takes the final phrase of d y├│ d├бd─Б┼Ыad asmai as expressing the indirect object with dad─Бti in b (тАЬgives [to him,] who тАжтАЭ), rather than as a qualification of v─лr├бm (or even of pitс╣Ы-, as Renou almost seems to). I think this is correct, but it is mildly disturbing that there is no overt expression of the datival recipient in the main clause; we would expect t├бsmai (see GeldnerтАЩs n. 20d). It may have been gapped because of the asmai in the rel. clause. Note that asmai cannot be a part of the main clause and refer to the indirect object, the man who does pious service, because it is unaccented; it must be part of the rel. cl. and refer to Soma.

+Griffith

To him who worships Soma gives the milch-cow, a fleet steed and a man of active knowledge,
Skilled in home duties, meet for holy synod, for council meet, a glory to his father.

+Geldner

Soma schenkt dem, der ihm opfert, eine Milchkuh, Soma ein rasches Streitro├Я, Soma einen werkt├╝chtigen Sohn, der im Haus, im Rat der Weisen, in der Versammlung t├╝chtig ist, der dem Vater Ruhm bringt.

+Grassmann

Die Kuh schenkt Soma, schnelle Rosse Soma, er schenkt den Sohn, der t├╝chtig ist im Werke, Im Hause t├╝chtig, in dem Fest, im Rathe, den V├дtern ruhmvoll, der dem Soma huldigt.

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe rejoice, Soma, contemplating you, invincible in battle, triumphant amongst hosts, the granter of heaven, the giver of rain, the preserver of strength, born amidst sacrifices, occupying a brilliant dwelling, renowned and victorious.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Invincible in combats, in battles a deliverer, winning the sun, winning the waters, herdsman of the community,
born at raids, granting good dwelling and good fame, conqueringтАФyou would we celebrate, o Soma.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse plays a minor syntactic trick. It consists of a string of acc. sg.

masc. qualifiers; since the previous vs. also consists largely of an acc. sg. masc. NP headed by v─лr├бm, the audience would be likely to assume that the new series of grammatically matching adjectives are also qualifiers of v─лr├бm, esp. since this type of syntactic dependence between verses is not uncommon in the RV. It is only when we arrive at the middle of the final p─Бda that we encounter tv─Б╠Бm and discover that the accusatives of this verse refer to Soma, not to the hero he gives us in 22.

Geldner accounts for the curious hapax bhareс╣гu-j─Б╠Б- тАШborn at raidsтАЩ by the fact that soma is especially offered before battle. This is probably correct, though the semantics could be tighter. Scarlatta essentially accepts this explanation and cites III.51.8 (of soma) j─Бt├бm тАж mah├й bh├бr─Бya, though he explores some other possibilities as well.

+Griffith

Invincible in fight, saver in battles, guard of our camp, winner of light and water,
Born amid hymns, well-housed, exceeding famous, victor, in thee will we rejoice, O Soma.

+Geldner

Wir m├╢chten dir, Soma, zujubeln als dem Sieger, der in den K├дmpfen unbezwungen, in den Schlachten heraushilft, der das Himmelslicht gewinnt, das Wasser gewinnt, dem Hirten der Opferpartei, dem Kampfgeborenen, der gute Wohnsitze, guten Ruhm erwirbt.

+Grassmann

Dich der du beistehst unbesiegt in Schlachten, verschaffend Glanz und Wasser, Wohnung schirmend, Zum Kampf geboren, sch├╢n an Ruhm und Wohnsitz, dich Sieger, Soma, wollen wir begr├╝ssen.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Soma, have genitive rated all these herbs, the water and the kine; you have spread out the spacious firmament; you have scattered darkness with light.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

You, Soma, begot all these plants here; you the waters, you the cows. You have stretched across the wide midspace; you have uncovered the darkness with your light.

+Griffith

These herbs, these milch-kine, and these running waters, all these, O Soma, thou hast generated.
The spacious firmament hast thou expanded, and with the light thou hast dispelled the darkness.

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDivine and potent Soma, bestow upon us, with your brilliant mind, a portion of wealth; may no (adversary) annoy you; you are supreme over the valour of (any) two (mutual) opponents; defend us (from our enemies) in battle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Allusions to Soma, the product of the earth and Soma, the moon

+Jamison Brereton

With your god(like) mind, god Soma, battle for a share of wealth for us, mighty one.
DonтАЩt let it hold out on you. You are master of heroism. On behalf of both (men and gods? / singers and patrons?) be on the lookout in the quest for cattle.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

In the phrase dev├йna тАж m├бnas─Б we again confront a noun (dev├б-) that seems to be used adjectivally (see vs. 14 above). I have half given in to this temptation, with тАЬgod(like).тАЭ The verb ─Б╠Бtanat in c poses some difficulties in interpretation. Surprisingly, none of the standard tr. who discuss the phrase notes that the same lexeme (─Б╠БтИЪtan) appears in the previous verse (22c) in the same metrical position and in a common, almost clich├йd╠Б usage. I think that ─Б╠Бtanat here is a slangy expression, deliberately constrasting with the high-style cosmic-description usage of ─Б╠Бtatantha in 22. I take the subject to be the wealth (or share of wealth) of b, rather than the m├бnas- of a, as Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take it, nor would I following Renou in taking it as an impersonal construction.

It is not entirely clear who the тАЬbothтАЭ are in d: Geldner singers and patrons, Renou men and gods.

Geldner supplies тАШpathтАЩ with pr├б cikits─Б (тАЬsei тАж der PfadfinderтАЭ) on the basis of IV.47.20. This is possible, and might even be supported by the panth─Б╠Бm in vs. 1, since pr├б cikits─Б seems to form a slight ring with pr├б cikitaс╕е in 1a. However, the verb does not need an object, in my opinion; the desiderative here can express a general intention to be alertly perceptive.

+Griffith

Do thou, God Soma, with thy Godlike spirit, victorious, win for us a share of riches.
Let none prevent thee: thou art Lord of valour. Provide for both sides in the fray for booty.
